  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

I do amended Gram-Schmidt for the blocks of Y to produce blocks of Q, but while Q would end up orthonormal, i am not sure that Q and Y would end up spanning the same space. Although the fact that Y is random product means Q may also be more or less random basis so maybe it doesn\'t matter so much that span(Q)=exactly span(Y).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSecond concern is still the situation when last split producted by MR doesn\'t have minimally sufficient k+p records of A for producing orthogonal Q. The ideal outcome is then just to add it to another split, but i can\'t figure an easy enough way to do that within MR framework (esp. if the input is serialized using compressed sequence file). one way is to do custom split indexing based on # of records encountered (similar to what that lzo MR project does). but it sounds too complicated to me. Another way is just to do a pre-pass over A and prepartition it the way that this condition is satisfied. Then have a custom split so that there\'s 1 mapper per partition. But that\'s still one additional preprocessing step which we\'d make just for the sake of just a fraction of A. Ideas are welcome here.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12917010_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'01\\/Oct\\/10 19:22\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-10-01T19:22:41+0000\'\u003e01\\/Oct\\/10 19:22\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I have couple of doubts. But that\'s still one additional preprocessing step which we\'d make just for the sake of just a fraction of A. \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12917392_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'03\\/Oct\\/10 20:17\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-10-03T20:17:09+0000\'\u003e03\\/Oct\\/10 20:17\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eAnother detail in Q computation: \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFor now we assume that Q=(1\\/L)Q\', where Q\' is the output of block orthonormalization, and L is the number of blocks we ended up with.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, in case when A is rather sparse, some Y blocks may not end up spanning R^(k+p) in which case orthogonalization would not produce normal columns. It doesn\'t mean that we can\'t orthonormalize the entire Y though. It just means that L is not for the entire Q but rather is individual for every column vector of Q and our initial assumption Q=(1\\/L)Q\' doesn\'t always hold.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWhich is fine per se, but then it means that there are perhaps quite frequent exceptions to assumption B =(1\\/L) Q\'^transpose * A. It would be easy to compute B^transpose in the same map-reduce pass as Q using multiple outputs , one for Q and one for B-transpose (which is what i am doing right now). But unless there\'s any workaround for the problem above, this B^transpose is incorrect for some sparse cases.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eTed, any thoughts? Thank you.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n-Dima\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12917392_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'03\\/Oct\\/10 20:17\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-10-03T20:17:09+0000\'\u003e03\\/Oct\\/10 20:17\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Another detail in Q computation:  \\n\\n For now we assume that Q=(1\\/L)Q\', where Q\' is the output of block orthonormalization, and L is the number of blocks we ended up with. \\n\\n However, in case when A is rather sparse, some Y blocks may not end up spanning R^(k+p) in which case orthogonalization would not produce normal columns. It doesn\'t mean that we can\'t orthonormalize the entire Y though. It just means that L is not for the entire Q but rather is individual for every column vector of Q and our initial assumption Q=(1\\/L)Q\' doesn\'t always hold. \\n\\n Which is fine per se, but then it means that there are perhaps quite frequent exceptions to assumption B =(1\\/L) Q\'^transpose * A. It would be easy to compute B^transpose in the same map-reduce pass as Q using multiple outputs , one for Q and one for B-transpose (which is what i am doing right now). But unless there\'s any workaround for the problem above, this B^transpose is incorrect for some sparse cases. \\n\\n Ted, any thoughts? Thank you. \\n-Dima              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12917394\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/MAHOUT-376?focusedCommentId=12917394&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12917394\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"tdunning\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12917394_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=tdunning\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"tdunning\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Ted Dunning\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - Dunning\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12920369_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Oct\\/10 21:55\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-10-12T21:55:31+0000\'\u003e12\\/Oct\\/10 21:55\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eDima,\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI just attached an update to the original outline document I posted.  The gist of it is that the Q_i need to be arranged in block diagonal form in order to form a bases of A\\\\Omega.  When that is done, my experiments show complete agreement with the original algorithm.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHere is R code that demonstrates decomposition without blocking and a 2 way block decomposition:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003e# SVD decompose a matrix, extracting the first k singular values\\/vectors\\n# using k+p random projection\\nsvd.rp = function(A, k=10, p=5) {\\n  n = nrow(A)\\n  y = A %*% matrix(rnorm(n * (k+p)), nrow=n)\\n  q = qr.Q(qr(y))\\n  b = t(q) %*% A\\n  svd = svd(b)\\n  list(u=q%*%svd$u, d=svd$d, v=svd$v)\\n}\\n\\n# block-wise SVD decompose a matrix, extracting the first k singular values\\/vectors\\n# using k+p random projection\\nsvd.rpx = function(A, k=10, p=5) {\\n  n = nrow(A)\\n  # block sizes\\n  n1 = floor(n\\/2)\\n  n2 = n-n1\\n\\n  r = matrix(rnorm(n * (k+p)), nrow=n)\\n  A1 = A[1:n1,]\\n  A2 = A[(n1+1):n,]\\n\\n  # block-wise multiplication and basis\\n  y1 = A1 %*% r\\n  q1 = qr.Q(qr(y1))\\n\\n  y2 = A2 %*% r\\n  q2 = qr.Q(qr(y2))\\n\\n  # construction of full q (not really necessary)\\n  z1 = diag(0, nrow=nrow(q1), ncol=(k+p))\\n  z2 = diag(0, nrow=nrow(q2), ncol=(k+p))\\n  q = rbind(cbind(q1, z1), cbind(z2, q2))\\n  b = t(q) %*% A\\n\\n  # we can compute b without forming the block diagonal Q\\n  bx = rbind(t(q1)%*%A1, t(q2)%*%A2)\\n\\n  # now the decomposition continues\\n  svd = svd(bx)\\n\\n  # \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003ereturn\u003c\\/span\u003e all the pieces \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003efor\u003c\\/span\u003e checking\\n  list(u=q%*%svd$u, d=svd$d, v=svd$v, q1=q1, q2=q2, q=q, b=b, bx=bx)\\n}\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eNote that this code has a fair bit of fat in it for debugging or illustrative purposes.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"tdunning\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Ted Dunning\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12920369_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'12\\/Oct\\/10 21:55\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-10-12T21:55:31+0000\'\u003e12\\/Oct\\/10 21:55\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Dima, \\n\\n I just attached an update to the original outline document I posted.  The gist of it is that the Q_i need to be arranged in block diagonal form in order to form a bases of A\\\\Omega.  When that is done, my experiments show complete agreement with the original algorithm.   \\n\\n Here is R code that demonstrates decomposition without blocking and a 2 way block decomposition: \\n  \\n # SVD decompose a matrix, extracting the first k singular values\\/vectors\\n# using k+p random projection\\nsvd.rp = function(A, k=10, p=5) {\\n  n = nrow(A)\\n  y = A %*% matrix(rnorm(n * (k+p)), nrow=n)\\n  q = qr.Q(qr(y))\\n  b = t(q) %*% A\\n  svd = svd(b)\\n  list(u=q%*%svd$u, d=svd$d, v=svd$v)\\n}\\n\\n# block-wise SVD decompose a matrix, extracting the first k singular values\\/vectors\\n# using k+p random projection\\nsvd.rpx = function(A, k=10, p=5) {\\n  n = nrow(A)\\n  # block sizes\\n  n1 = floor(n\\/2)\\n  n2 = n-n1\\n\\n  r = matrix(rnorm(n * (k+p)), nrow=n)\\n  A1 = A[1:n1,]\\n  A2 = A[(n1+1):n,]\\n\\n  # block-wise multiplication and basis\\n  y1 = A1 %*% r\\n  q1 = qr.Q(qr(y1))\\n\\n  y2 = A2 %*% r\\n  q2 = qr.Q(qr(y2))\\n\\n  # construction of full q (not really necessary)\\n  z1 = diag(0, nrow=nrow(q1), ncol=(k+p))\\n  z2 = diag(0, nrow=nrow(q2), ncol=(k+p))\\n  q = rbind(cbind(q1, z1), cbind(z2, q2))\\n  b = t(q) %*% A\\n\\n  # we can compute b without forming the block diagonal Q\\n  bx = rbind(t(q1)%*%A1, t(q2)%*%A2)\\n\\n  # now the decomposition continues\\n  svd = svd(bx)\\n\\n  #  return  all the pieces  for  checking\\n  list(u=q%*%svd$u, d=svd$d, v=svd$v, q1=q1, q2=q2, q=q, b=b, bx=bx)\\n}\\n \\n  \\n Note that this code has a fair bit of fat in it for debugging or illustrative purposes. \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12965608_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'01\\/Dec\\/10 08:28\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-01T08:28:16+0000\'\u003e01\\/Dec\\/10 08:28\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"dlyubimov2 - 01\\/Dec\\/10 08:36\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eyes, it is 100% streaming in terms of A and Y rows. Assumption is that we are ok to load one A row into memory at a time and we optimize for tall matrices (such as billion by million) So we are bound at n but not at m from memory point of view.  Even if it is dense, one such vector would take 8MB memory at a time. but sparse sequential vectors should be ok too (it will probably require a little tweak during Y computations to scan it one time sequentially instead of k+p times as i think it is done now with assumption it can be random).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFor memory, the concern is random access q blocks which can be no less than k+p by k+p (that is, for the case of k+p=500, it gets to be 2 Mb). But this is all as far as memory is concerned. (well actually 2 times that, plus there\'s a Y lookahead buffer in order to make sure we can safely form next block. Plus there\'s a packed R. so for k+p=500 it looks like minimum memory requirement is rougly in the area of 7-8Mb. which is well below anything). \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eY lookahead buffer is not a requirement of algorithm itself, it\'s MR specific, to make sure we have at least k+p rows to process in the split before we start next block. i thought about it but not much; at 2mb minimum dense memory requirement it did not strike me as a big issue.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eCPU may be more of a problem, it is quadratic, as in any QR algorithm known to me. but i am actually not sure if Givens series would produce more crunching than e.g. Householder\'s . Givens certainly is as numerically stable as householder\'s and better than Gramm-Schmidt. In my tests for 100k tall matrix the orthonormality residuals seem to hold at about  no less than 10e-13 and surprisingly i did not notice any degradataion at all compared to smaller sizes.  Actually I happened to read aobut  LAPack methods ithat  prefer Givens for possiblity of re-ordering and thus easier parallelization). \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAnyway, speaking of numerical stability, whatever degradation occurs, i think it would be dwarfed by stochastic inaccuracy which grows quite significantly in my low rank tests. Perhaps for kp=500 it should degrade much less than for 20-30.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBut i guess we need to test at scale to see the limitations.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12965608_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'01\\/Dec\\/10 08:28\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-01T08:28:16+0000\'\u003e01\\/Dec\\/10 08:28\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"dlyubimov2 - 01\\/Dec\\/10 08:36\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   yes, it is 100% streaming in terms of A and Y rows. Assumption is that we are ok to load one A row into memory at a time and we optimize for tall matrices (such as billion by million) So we are bound at n but not at m from memory point of view.  Even if it is dense, one such vector would take 8MB memory at a time. but sparse sequential vectors should be ok too (it will probably require a little tweak during Y computations to scan it one time sequentially instead of k+p times as i think it is done now with assumption it can be random). \\n\\n For memory, the concern is random access q blocks which can be no less than k+p by k+p (that is, for the case of k+p=500, it gets to be 2 Mb). But this is all as far as memory is concerned. (well actually 2 times that, plus there\'s a Y lookahead buffer in order to make sure we can safely form next block. Plus there\'s a packed R. so for k+p=500 it looks like minimum memory requirement is rougly in the area of 7-8Mb. which is well below anything).  \\n\\n Y lookahead buffer is not a requirement of algorithm itself, it\'s MR specific, to make sure we have at least k+p rows to process in the split before we start next block. i thought about it but not much; at 2mb minimum dense memory requirement it did not strike me as a big issue. \\n\\n CPU may be more of a problem, it is quadratic, as in any QR algorithm known to me. but i am actually not sure if Givens series would produce more crunching than e.g. Householder\'s . Givens certainly is as numerically stable as householder\'s and better than Gramm-Schmidt. In my tests for 100k tall matrix the orthonormality residuals seem to hold at about  no less than 10e-13 and surprisingly i did not notice any degradataion at all compared to smaller sizes.  Actually I happened to read aobut  LAPack methods ithat  prefer Givens for possiblity of re-ordering and thus easier parallelization).  \\n\\n Anyway, speaking of numerical stability, whatever degradation occurs, i think it would be dwarfed by stochastic inaccuracy which grows quite significantly in my low rank tests. Perhaps for kp=500 it should degrade much less than for 20-30. \\n\\n But i guess we need to test at scale to see the limitations.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12965742\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/MAHOUT-376?focusedCommentId=12965742&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12965742\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12965742_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'01\\/Dec\\/10 16:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-01T16:52:55+0000\'\u003e01\\/Dec\\/10 16:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"dlyubimov2 - 02\\/Dec\\/10 01:34\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eThere is a catch though. With this implementation, m is memory bound. It is not in mapper though but in combiners and mapper of the next step. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBut my reasoning was, with 1G memory and k+p =500 it seems to exist rather wide spectrum of admissible combinations of r (block height) and minSplitSize (governing essentually # of mappers needed) that would cover billion rows, and the sweet spot of this combination seem to exceed 1 bln rows. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIn addition, there are 2 remedies to consider. First is rather straightforward application of compression on R sequence. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSecond remedy results from the fact that our QR merge process is hierarchical. Right now it\'s two-level hierarchy. I.e if processes at each stage merge 1000 q blocks, then at the next level we can merge another 1000 q blocks, so total number of q blocks is thus approx. 1 mln. (for 1G memory the number of some 600-800k blocks is more plausible). Assuming Q blocks are k+p rows high, that gives us aprroximately 300 mln rows for m. But the trick is that if we have 1G memory in the mapper, then Q blocks don\'t have to be 500 rows high, then can easily be 200k rows high. Which immediately puts us in the range, conservatively, of 10 bln rows or so without any additional remedies, which i think is about the scale of Google\'s document index in 2005, if we wanted to do an LSI on it, assuming there\'s 1 mln lemmas in English, which there\'s not. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBut if we add another map-only pass over blocked Q data, then we can have 1 bln blocks with all the considerations above and that should put us in the range of 30 trillion rows of A. This number grows exponentially with every added MR pass which is why i am saying m is virtually unbound. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAdding these remedies seems to be pretty straighforward, but for a first stab at the problem my estimates for m bound seem to be adequate. With these kind of numbers, this may easily become a technology in a search of a problem. We may add some analysis on optimality of combination of block size and minSplitSize. My initial thought is that finding maximum here is pretty straigtoward, seems to be a task of finding maximum on a second degree polynomial function.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt\'s more likely that much more memory would go into precision effort rather than maximizing m bound though. E.g. instead of covering the scale, the resources may go into increasing precision and oversampling. In which case additional map-only passes over Q will be tremendously useful. (imagine this could do k+p=5000 with just one additional map-only pass over Q data) If this is the case, then the next low hanging fruit step is to add map-only hierarchical merge of Rs on Q blocks.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, it\'s a stochastic algorithm and as such it is probably not good enough for processes that would require such precision (e.g certainly not to do math work on rocket boosters, i think). That said, k+p=5000 probably doesn\'t make sense. I think applications sharply divide into 2 categories, where precision requirements are either much higher than that, or much lower. I can\'t think of much in between. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eApologies  for multiple editions, mostly typos and correction to numbers. These numbers are still pretty offhand and exercise in mental arithmetics, actual mileage probably will vary as much as +- 40% because of unaccounted overhead. I tried to be conservative though.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12965742_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'01\\/Dec\\/10 16:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-01T16:52:55+0000\'\u003e01\\/Dec\\/10 16:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"dlyubimov2 - 02\\/Dec\\/10 01:34\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   There is a catch though. With this implementation, m is memory bound. It is not in mapper though but in combiners and mapper of the next step.  \\n\\n But my reasoning was, with 1G memory and k+p =500 it seems to exist rather wide spectrum of admissible combinations of r (block height) and minSplitSize (governing essentually # of mappers needed) that would cover billion rows, and the sweet spot of this combination seem to exceed 1 bln rows.  \\n\\n In addition, there are 2 remedies to consider. First is rather straightforward application of compression on R sequence.  \\n\\n Second remedy results from the fact that our QR merge process is hierarchical. Right now it\'s two-level hierarchy. I.e if processes at each stage merge 1000 q blocks, then at the next level we can merge another 1000 q blocks, so total number of q blocks is thus approx. 1 mln. (for 1G memory the number of some 600-800k blocks is more plausible). Assuming Q blocks are k+p rows high, that gives us aprroximately 300 mln rows for m. But the trick is that if we have 1G memory in the mapper, then Q blocks don\'t have to be 500 rows high, then can easily be 200k rows high. Which immediately puts us in the range, conservatively, of 10 bln rows or so without any additional remedies, which i think is about the scale of Google\'s document index in 2005, if we wanted to do an LSI on it, assuming there\'s 1 mln lemmas in English, which there\'s not.  \\n\\n But if we add another map-only pass over blocked Q data, then we can have 1 bln blocks with all the considerations above and that should put us in the range of 30 trillion rows of A. This number grows exponentially with every added MR pass which is why i am saying m is virtually unbound.  \\n\\n Adding these remedies seems to be pretty straighforward, but for a first stab at the problem my estimates for m bound seem to be adequate. With these kind of numbers, this may easily become a technology in a search of a problem. We may add some analysis on optimality of combination of block size and minSplitSize. My initial thought is that finding maximum here is pretty straigtoward, seems to be a task of finding maximum on a second degree polynomial function. \\n\\n It\'s more likely that much more memory would go into precision effort rather than maximizing m bound though. E.g. instead of covering the scale, the resources may go into increasing precision and oversampling. In which case additional map-only passes over Q will be tremendously useful. (imagine this could do k+p=5000 with just one additional map-only pass over Q data) If this is the case, then the next low hanging fruit step is to add map-only hierarchical merge of Rs on Q blocks. \\n\\n However, it\'s a stochastic algorithm and as such it is probably not good enough for processes that would require such precision (e.g certainly not to do math work on rocket boosters, i think). That said, k+p=5000 probably doesn\'t make sense. I think applications sharply divide into 2 categories, where precision requirements are either much higher than that, or much lower. I can\'t think of much in between.  \\n\\n Apologies  for multiple editions, mostly typos and correction to numbers. These numbers are still pretty offhand and exercise in mental arithmetics, actual mileage probably will vary as much as +- 40% because of unaccounted overhead. I tried to be conservative though.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12965961\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/MAHOUT-376?focusedCommentId=12965961&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12965961\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - If we don\'t do that, it will cause a lot of IO in mappers and kind of defeats the purpose of MR imo.  \\n\\n I think that my suggested approach handles this already. \\n\\n The block decomposition of Q via the blockwise QR decomposition implies a breakdown of B into column-wise blocks which can each be handled separately.  The results are then combined using concatenation. \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12966223\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/MAHOUT-376?focusedCommentId=12966223&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12966223\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966223_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 18:32\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T18:32:36+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 18:32\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eI think that my suggested approach handles this already.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe block decomposition of Q via the blockwise QR decomposition implies a breakdown of B into column-wise blocks which can each be handled separately. The results are then combined using concatenation.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eTed, yes, i understand that part, but i think we are talking about different things. What I am talking about is formation of Y rows well before orthonotmalization is even concerned. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWhat i mean is that right now VectorWritable loads the entire thing into memory. Hence, the bound for width of A. (i.e. we can\'t load A row that is longer than some memory chunk we can afford for it). \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, what A row is participating in in each case is a bunch of (namely, k+p) dot-products. In order to produce those, it is sufficient to examine A row sequentialy  (i.e. streamingly) in one pass while keeping only k+p values in memory as dot-accumulators.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHence,  say if we equipped VectorWritable with a push-parser like element handler (notorious DocumentHanlder immediately pops in memory form SAXParser) then we will never have to examine more than one element of A row at a time. And hence we are not bound by memory for n (A width) anymore. That handler would form Y rows directly during the sequential examination of A rows. Identical considerations are in effect when forming Qt*A partial products (i already checked for this).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI already thought about this approach a little (and i believe Jake Mannix also posted something very similar to that recently to effect of sequential vector examination backed by a streaming read). \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSince it is touching VectorWritable internals, i think i would need to make a change proposal for it and if seems reasonable handle it in another issue. I will do so but i need to check couple of things first in Hadoop see if it is feasible within current MR framework and doesn\'t blow off all benefits code-data collocation.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf that proposal is implemented, and MR considerations are tackled, we will have SSVD that scales to about a billion rows for 500 singular vlaues and 1G memory in mapper vertically (m) and a gazillion in n (width). \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ntheoretically. How about that.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966223_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 18:32\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T18:32:36+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 18:32\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     I think that my suggested approach handles this already. \\n\\n The block decomposition of Q via the blockwise QR decomposition implies a breakdown of B into column-wise blocks which can each be handled separately. The results are then combined using concatenation. \\n \\n Ted, yes, i understand that part, but i think we are talking about different things. What I am talking about is formation of Y rows well before orthonotmalization is even concerned.  \\n\\n What i mean is that right now VectorWritable loads the entire thing into memory. Hence, the bound for width of A. (i.e. we can\'t load A row that is longer than some memory chunk we can afford for it).  \\n\\n However, what A row is participating in in each case is a bunch of (namely, k+p) dot-products. In order to produce those, it is sufficient to examine A row sequentialy  (i.e. streamingly) in one pass while keeping only k+p values in memory as dot-accumulators. \\n\\n Hence,  say if we equipped VectorWritable with a push-parser like element handler (notorious DocumentHanlder immediately pops in memory form SAXParser) then we will never have to examine more than one element of A row at a time. And hence we are not bound by memory for n (A width) anymore. That handler would form Y rows directly during the sequential examination of A rows. Identical considerations are in effect when forming Qt*A partial products (i already checked for this). \\n\\n I already thought about this approach a little (and i believe Jake Mannix also posted something very similar to that recently to effect of sequential vector examination backed by a streaming read).  \\n\\n Since it is touching VectorWritable internals, i think i would need to make a change proposal for it and if seems reasonable handle it in another issue. I will do so but i need to check couple of things first in Hadoop see if it is feasible within current MR framework and doesn\'t blow off all benefits code-data collocation. \\n\\n If that proposal is implemented, and MR considerations are tackled, we will have SSVD that scales to about a billion rows for 500 singular vlaues and 1G memory in mapper vertically (m) and a gazillion in n (width).  \\ntheoretically. How about that. \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12966229\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/MAHOUT-376?focusedCommentId=12966229&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12966229\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"tdunning\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12966229_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=tdunning\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"tdunning\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Ted Dunning\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - (i.e. we can\'t load A row that is longer than some memory chunk we can afford for it).\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI understand that now.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe current limitation is that the sparse representation of a row has to fit into memory.  That means that we are limited to cases with a few hundred million non-zero elements and are effectively unlimited on the number of potential columns of A.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe only other place that the total  number of elements in a row comes into play is in B.  Using the block form of Q, however, we never\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nhave to store an entire row of B, just manageable chunks.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eMy real worry with your approach is that the average number of elements per row of A is likely to be comparable to p+k.  This means that Y = A \\\\Omega will be about as large as A.  Processing that sequentially is a non-starter and the computation of Q without block QR means that Y is processed sequentially.  On the other hand, if we block decompose Y, we want blocks that fit into memory because that block size lives on in B and all subsequent steps.  Thus, streaming QR is a non-issue in a blocked implementation.  The blocked implementation gives a natural parallel implementation.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"tdunning\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12966229_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=tdunning\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"tdunning\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Ted Dunning\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966229_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 18:48\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T18:48:59+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 18:48\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    \\n &gt; I think that my suggested approach handles this already. \\n\\n &gt; The block decomposition of Q via the blockwise QR decomposition implies a breakdown of B into column-wise blocks which  \\n&gt; can each be handled separately. (i.e. we can\'t load A row that is longer than some memory chunk we can afford for it).  \\n\\n I understand that now. \\n\\n The current limitation is that the sparse representation of a row has to fit into memory.  That means that we are limited to cases with a few hundred million non-zero elements and are effectively unlimited on the number of potential columns of A. \\n\\n The only other place that the total  number of elements in a row comes into play is in B.  Using the block form of Q, however, we never \\nhave to store an entire row of B, just manageable chunks. \\n\\n My real worry with your approach is that the average number of elements per row of A is likely to be comparable to p+k. On the other hand, if we block decompose Y, we want blocks that fit into memory because that block size lives on in B and all subsequent steps.  Thus, streaming QR is a non-issue in a blocked implementation. \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966265_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 20:22\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T20:22:18+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 20:22\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"dlyubimov2 - 02\\/Dec\\/10 20:26\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eMy real worry with your approach is that the average number of elements per row of A is likely to be comparable to p+k. This means that Y = A \\\\Omega will be about as large as A. Processing that sequentially is a non-starter and the computation of Q without block QR means that Y is processed sequentially. On the other hand, if we block decompose Y, we want blocks that fit into memory because that block size lives on in B and all subsequent steps. Thus, streaming QR is a non-issue in a blocked implementation. The blocked implementation gives a natural parallel implementation.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI think you misunderstanding it a little. the actual implementation is not that naive. let me clarify. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFirst, there \u003cb\u003eis\u003c\\/b\u003e blocking. More over, it\'s a hierarchical blocking. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ethe way it works, you specify block height, which is more k+p but ideally less than a MR split would host (you can specify more but you may be producing some network traffic then to move non-collocated parts of the split). Blocks are considered completely in parallel.  Hence, initial parallelizm degree is m\\/r where r is average block height. They can (and are) considered independently, among the splits. \\\"thin streaming QR\\\" runs \u003cb\u003einside\u003c\\/b\u003e the blocks, not on the whole Y. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSecondly, Y matrix, or even its blocks, are never formed. What is formed is shifting intermediate Q buffer of the size (k+p)xr and intermediate upper triangular R of size (k+p)x(k+p). Since they are triangular, there\'s a rudimental implementation of Matrix itnerface called UpperTriangular not to waste space on lower triangle but still allow random access.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThirdly, the hierarchy. when we form Q blocks, we will have to update them with Givens operations resulting from merging R matrices. This is done in combiner and this  comes very natural to it. If there\'s say z blocks in a mapper then Q1 goes thru updates resulting from z merges of R, Q2 goes thru udpates resulting from z-1 merges and so on. Nothing being concatenated (or unblocked) there except for the R sequence (but it is still sequence, that is sequentially accessed thing) which i already provided memory estimates for. Most importantly, it does not depend on the block height, so you can shrink R sequence length if you have higher Q blocks, but higher Q blocks also take more memory to process at a time. there\'s a sweet spot to be hit here with parameters defining block height and split size, so it maximizes the thruput. for k+p=500 i don\'t see any memory concerns there in a single combiner run. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAnd there\'s no reducer (i.e. any sizable shuffle and sort) here. At the end of this operation we have a bunch of Rs which corresponds to the number of splits, and a bunch of interbediate Q blocks still same size which correspond to number of Q-blocks. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eNow we can repeat this process  hierarchically with additional map-only passes over Q blocks until only one R block is left. with 1G memory, as i said, my estimate is we can merge up to 1000 Rs \u003cb\u003eper combiner\u003c\\/b\u003e with one MR pass (without extra overhead for single Q block and other java things). (in reality in this implementation there are 2 levels in this hierarchy which seems to point to over 1 bln rows, or about 1 mln Q blocks of some relatively moderate height r&gt;&gt;k+p, but like i said with just one  map-only pass one can increase scale of m to single trillions ). This hierarchical merging is exactly what i meant by \'making MR work harder\' for us. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThere is a poor illustration of this hierarchical process in the doc that makes it perhaps more clear than words. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAlso let me point out that the fact that the processes involved in R merging are \u003cb\u003emap-only\u003c\\/b\u003e,  which means that if we play the splitting game right in MR, there would  \u003cb\u003epractically be no networking IO\u003c\\/b\u003e per MR theory. This is very important imo for such scale. The only IO that occurs is to \'slurp\' r sequences from HDFS before next stage of hierarchical R-merge. For a sequence of 1000 R, k+p 500, the size of R, dense and uncompressed, is approximately 1 mb each, so for a sequence of thousand Rs, the size of such slurp IO, dense and uncompressed,  would be 1G, which is less than what i am having today in a single step with Pig for a 200k of proto-packed log records today in production and that finishes in a minute.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBottom line, let\'s benchmark it. So we don\'t have to guess. Especially if we can do  A vector streaming. I am personally having trouble with logistics of this so far, as i mentioned before. I will get to benchmarking it sooner or later. Important thing for me at this point was to make sure it does correct computation (which it does) and make educated guess about the scale (which is billion by million without vector streaming support or billion to gazillion with vector streaming support, with potential to extend m scale thousand times with each additional map-only pass over Q data (which is (k+p)xm which is again unbounded for n).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ethanks. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - If there\'s say z blocks in a mapper then Q1 goes thru updates resulting from z merges of R, Q2 goes thru udpates resulting from z-1 merges and so on. Most importantly, it does not depend on the block height, so you can shrink R sequence length if you have higher Q blocks, but higher Q blocks also take more memory to process at a time. there\'s a sweet spot to be hit here with parameters defining block height and split size, so it maximizes the thruput. for k+p=500 i don\'t see any memory concerns there in a single combiner run.  \\n\\n And there\'s no reducer (i.e. any sizable shuffle and sort) here. (in reality in this implementation there are 2 levels in this hierarchy which seems to point to over 1 bln rows, or about 1 mln Q blocks of some relatively moderate height r&gt;&gt;k+p, but like i said with just one  map-only pass one can increase scale of m to single trillions ). This hierarchical merging is exactly what i meant by \'making MR work harder\' for us.  \\n\\n There is a poor illustration of this hierarchical process in the doc that makes it perhaps more clear than words.  \\n\\n Also let me point out that the fact that the processes involved in R merging are  map-only ,  which means that if we play the splitting game right in MR, there would   practically be no networking IO  per MR theory. This is very important imo for such scale. The only IO that occurs is to \'slurp\' r sequences from HDFS before next stage of hierarchical R-merge. I will get to benchmarking it sooner or later. sizable shuffle and sort) here. At the end of this operation we have a bunch of Rs which corresponds to the number of splits, and a bunch of interbediate Q blocks still same size which correspond to number of Q-blocks.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eNow we can repeat this process hierarchically with additional map-only passes over Q blocks until only one R block is left. with 1G memory, as i said, my estimate is we can merge up to 1000 Rs per combiner with one MR pass (without extra overhead for single Q block and other java things). (in reality in this implementation there are 2 levels in this hierarchy which seems to point to over 1 bln rows, or about 1 mln Q blocks of some relatively moderate height r&gt;&gt;k+p, but like i said with just one map-only pass one can increase scale of m to single trillions ). This hierarchical merging is exactly what i meant by \'making MR work harder\' for us.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSounds to me like the reducer could replicate the combiner and thus implement the second step of your hierarchy which would avoid the second MR pass.  You could have a single reducer which receives all combiner outputs and thus merge everything.  Since you can\'t guarantee that the combiner does any work, this is best practice anyway.  The specification is that the combiner will run zero or more times.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis also raises the question of whether your combiner can be applied multiple times.  I suspect yes.  You will know better than I.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"tdunning\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12966297_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=tdunning\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"tdunning\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Ted Dunning\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966297_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 21:56\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T21:56:16+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 21:56\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    \\n I think you misunderstanding it a little. the actual implementation is not that naive. let me clarify.  \\n\\n I was hoping I misunderstood it. \\n\\n \\n And there\'s no reducer (i.e. any sizable shuffle and sort) here. At the end of this operation we have a bunch of Rs which corresponds to the number of splits, and a bunch of interbediate Q blocks still same size which correspond to number of Q-blocks. \\n\\n Now we can repeat this process hierarchically with additional map-only passes over Q blocks until only one R block is left. with 1G memory, as i said, my estimate is we can merge up to 1000 Rs per combiner with one MR pass (without extra overhead for single Q block and other java things). (in reality in this implementation there are 2 levels in this hierarchy which seems to point to over 1 bln rows, or about 1 mln Q blocks of some relatively moderate height r&gt;&gt;k+p, but like i said with just one map-only pass one can increase scale of m to single trillions ). This hierarchical merging is exactly what i meant by \'making MR work harder\' for us.  \\n\\n Sounds to me like the reducer could replicate the combiner and thus implement the second step of your hierarchy which would avoid the second MR pass.  You could have a single reducer which receives all combiner outputs and thus merge everything.  Since you can\'t guarantee that the combiner does any work, this is best practice anyway.  The specification is that the combiner will run zero or more times.   \\n\\n This also raises the question of whether your combiner can be applied multiple times.  I suspect yes.  You will know better than I.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12966333\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/MAHOUT-376?focusedCommentId=12966333&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-12966333\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966333_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 23:01\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T23:01:33+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 23:01\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"dlyubimov2 - 02\\/Dec\\/10 23:14\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eSounds to me like the reducer could replicate the combiner and thus implement the second step of your hierarchy which would avoid the second MR pass. You could have a single reducer which receives all combiner outputs and thus merge everything.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFirst of all, second level hierarchical merge  is done in Bt job mappers &#8211; so moving this code into reducer wouldn\'t actually really win anything in terms of actual IO or # of MR passes.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSecondly,  I don\'t beleive single reducer pass is efficient. All parallelization is gone, isn\'t it? But the problem is not even that but limitation on how many Rs you can preload for the merges into same process.  Rs are preloaded as a side info (and we relinquish one R with every Q we process in combiner, so initially it loads all but then throws them away one by one. So we can\'t merge them all in one pass, but we can divide them into subsequences. If they merged by subsequences, subsequences must be completed and order is important and should be exactly the same for all Q blocks. The catch is that each Q update has to complete the merges of the reminder of the R sequence. Such subsequence merge is described in computeQHatSequence algorithm in my notes.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFinally, there\'s no need to sort. When we do R merge, as it is shown in the notes, we have to revisit  Q blocks (and Rs) exactly in the same order we just produced them in. Problem is that when we revisit a Q block, we have to have the tail of all subsequent R blocks handy.  So even if we sent them to reducers (which was my initial plan), we\'d have to sort them by task id they came from and then by their order inside the task that produced them. And then we might need to duplicate R traffic to every reducer process. Huge waste, again.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003e Since you can\'t guarantee that the combiner does any work, this is best practice anyway. The specification is that the combiner will run zero or more times.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThat  actually is absolutely valid and i was very concerned about it in the beginning. I expected it but it did not turn up in tests so far, so that issue was  slowly glimmering in my subconsciousness ever since.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf that actually is a problem then yes I might be forced to extend Q pass to include reducer. Which IMO would be a humongous exercise in IO bandwidth waste. there\'s no need for that. there\'s only need a for local merge of R sequences and doing second pass over q block sequence  you just generated, in the same order you generated it. Even a combiner is an overshoot for that, if i were implementing it in a regular parallel batching way, since there\'s no need to reorder q blocks. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI also considered that If i am forced to address that i can still do it in the mapper only without even a combiner by pushing Q blocks to local FS side files and doing a second pass over them and that\'d be much more efficient than pushing them to another networked process. Not mentioning all the unneeded sorting involved in between and all the armtwisting i was struggling with involved in sending them in same task  chunks, same order. There\'s still rudimentary remainder of that attempt in the code (the key that carries task id and order id for Q block that are never subsequently used anywhere). But saving local side file in mapper and do second pass over it is still way more attractive than reducer approach if i need to fix this.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eThis also raises the question of whether your combiner can be applied multiple times. I suspect yes. You will know better than I.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eYes, that\'s the optional hierarchy increment that  i was talking about, that we can additionally implement if billion for m  and  unbound n is not good enough.  \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966333_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 23:01\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T23:01:33+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 23:01\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"dlyubimov2 - 02\\/Dec\\/10 23:14\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   \\n Sounds to me like the reducer could replicate the combiner and thus implement the second step of your hierarchy which would avoid the second MR pass. You could have a single reducer which receives all combiner outputs and thus merge everything.  \\n\\n First of all, second level hierarchical merge  is done in Bt job mappers &#8211; so moving this code into reducer wouldn\'t actually really win anything in terms of actual IO or # of MR passes. \\n\\n Secondly,  I don\'t beleive single reducer pass is efficient. All parallelization is gone, isn\'t it? But the problem is not even that but limitation on how many Rs you can preload for the merges into same process.  Rs are preloaded as a side info (and we relinquish one R with every Q we process in combiner, so initially it loads all but then throws them away one by one. So we can\'t merge them all in one pass, but we can divide them into subsequences. If they merged by subsequences, subsequences must be completed and order is important and should be exactly the same for all Q blocks. The catch is that each Q update has to complete the merges of the reminder of the R sequence. Such subsequence merge is described in computeQHatSequence algorithm in my notes. \\n\\n Finally, there\'s no need to sort. When we do R merge, as it is shown in the notes, we have to revisit  Q blocks (and Rs) exactly in the same order we just produced them in. Problem is that when we revisit a Q block, we have to have the tail of all subsequent R blocks handy.  So even if we sent them to reducers (which was my initial plan), we\'d have to sort them by task id they came from and then by their order inside the task that produced them. And then we might need to duplicate R traffic to every reducer process. Huge waste, again. \\n\\n \\n  Since you can\'t guarantee that the combiner does any work, this is best practice anyway. The specification is that the combiner will run zero or more times.  \\n\\n That  actually is absolutely valid and i was very concerned about it in the beginning. I expected it but it did not turn up in tests so far, so that issue was  slowly glimmering in my subconsciousness ever since.   \\n\\n If that actually is a problem then yes I might be forced to extend Q pass to include reducer. Which IMO would be a humongous exercise in IO bandwidth waste. there\'s no need for that. there\'s only need a for local merge of R sequences and doing second pass over q block sequence  you just generated, in the same order you generated it. Even a combiner is an overshoot for that, if i were implementing it in a regular parallel batching way, since there\'s no need to reorder q blocks.  \\n\\n I also considered that If i am forced to address that i can still do it in the mapper only without even a combiner by pushing Q blocks to local FS side files and doing a second pass over them and that\'d be much more efficient than pushing them to another networked process. Not mentioning all the unneeded sorting involved in between and all the armtwisting i was struggling with involved in sending them in same task  chunks, same order. There\'s still rudimentary remainder of that attempt in the code (the key that carries task id and order id for Q block that are never subsequently used anywhere). But saving local side file in mapper and do second pass over it is still way more attractive than reducer approach if i need to fix this. \\n\\n \\n This also raises the question of whether your combiner can be applied multiple times. I suspect yes. You will know better than I.  \\n\\n Yes, that\'s the optional hierarchy increment that  i was talking about, that we can additionally implement if billion for m  and  unbound n is not good enough. \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966352_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 23:50\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T23:50:24+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 23:50\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e only partially valid. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt all depends on what you are spec\'d to. say we are spec\'d to 1G + java\\/mr overhead, and few hundred million non-zero elements will take Which is already all or more than all i have.  In my spec, (million non-zeros) it\'s only 8 mb that\'s seems ok. SSVD assumption doesn\'t include any significant memory allocation for rows of A, and most importantly, it doesn\'t have to, i think.  Philosophy here is that A is a file, and read it with a buffer to optimize I\\/O, but my stream buffer doesn\'t have to be forced to be 1G on me. \u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10453\\\" alt=\\\"dlyubimov2\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e dlyubimov2\u003c\\/span\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12966352_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Dec\\/10 23:50\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-12-02T23:50:24+0000\'\u003e02\\/Dec\\/10 23:50\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     That means that we are limited to cases with a few hundred million non-zero elements and are effectively unlimited on the number of potential columns of A.  \\n\\n I beleive in case of SSVD this statement only partially valid.  \\n\\n It all depends on what you are spec\'d to. say we are spec\'d to 1G + java\\/mr overhead, and few hundred million non-zero elements will take few hundred megabytes multiplied by 8.
